**Phase 136 ÔÇö Complete.** All 289 test modules green. Sovereign Skew Heap (Sleator & Tarjan, 1986) ÔÇö a **self-adjusting meldable priority queue**, a new capability for the platform (no heap/priority-queue existed) and a thematic companion to the splay tree (both self-adjusting, no balance metadata). The single primitive is **meld**: keep the smaller of the two roots, meld its right subtree with the other heap, then **swap that root's children** ÔÇö the swap is what amortises the right-spine to `O(log n)` with no rank/height bookkeeping. `insert` melds a singleton, `extract_min` melds the root's two children, and `meld` unions two heaps wholesale (the operation an array binary-heap lacks). This implementation melds **iteratively** ÔÇö merging the two ascending right-spines into a sorted list and relinking from the back with the child-swap ÔÇö so it is **immune to Python recursion limits on adversarial inputs**. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against `heapq` over 15 000 interleaved insert/extract ops** matched every `extract_min`; `meld` of two heaps equals the sorted union; and **20 000 ascending (and 20 000 descending) inserts complete with no `RecursionError`**. Exposed at `/api/v1/skewheap`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/skew_heap_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- Ôťů 136A: `pradyos/core/skew_heap.py` ÔÇö `SkewHeapError(detail)`; `SkewHeap()` with `insert(value)` (duplicates allowed), `extract_min()` / `peek_min()` / `find_min()` (raise on empty), `meld(other)` (unions; empties `other`), `keys_sorted()` (read-only), `reset()`, `is_empty()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `kind` properties + `stats()`. Values must be one orderable kind (`int`/`float` or `str`); bools, non-orderable values, mixed-kind inserts and mismatched-kind melds raise `SkewHeapError`. The meld is iterative (no recursion-depth risk).
- Ôťů 136B: `pradyos/web/skew_heap_web.py` ÔÇö `register_skewheap_routes(app, skew_heap=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/skewheap/insert` (body `{value}`; 422 on missing / bad / mixed-kind), `POST /api/v1/skewheap/extract_min` (422 on empty), `GET /api/v1/skewheap/peek` (`min` null when empty), `GET /api/v1/skewheap/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/skewheap/reset` (`meld` stays on the core class).
- Ôťů 136C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase136.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `skew_heap` param, and a single `register_skewheap_routes(app, skew_heap)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- Ôťů 136D: `tests/test_skew_heap.py` (33) + `tests/test_skewheap_web.py` (19) ÔÇö priority-queue semantics (extract in sorted order, peek, keys_sorted, duplicates, floats, strings); **a differential test against `heapq`** over 15 000 interleaved ops; **adversarial 20 000 ascending & descending inserts** (no recursion error); **meld** (= sorted union, empties other, into/with empty, self-noop, kind-mismatch & non-heap raise); empty-op & validation raises (bool, non-orderable, mixed kind) + `SkewHeapError.detail`; determinism; `kind` resets when emptied; reset; 10-thread concurrent inserts; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `wavelet`).

**Phase 137 ÔÇö Complete.** All 291 test modules green. Sovereign Interval Tree (CormenÔÇôLeisersonÔÇôRivestÔÇôStein, augmented BST) ÔÇö a **dynamic set of intervals supporting overlap and stabbing queries**, a new capability for the platform. Intervals `[low, high]` (endpoints inclusive) are stored in a BST keyed by `low`, and every node is augmented with `max` ÔÇö the maximum `high` endpoint in its subtree ÔÇö which lets a search prune whole subtrees: to find an overlapping interval, descend left when the left subtree's `max` reaches the query's `low`, else right. Supports `insert`, `remove`, `contains`, `overlap_any(low, high)`, `overlap(low, high)` (all intersecting intervals, with subtree-`max` pruning), `stab(point)`, and `count`. Every operation is **iterative** (the augmentation is recomputed along the recorded path), so the tree is immune to recursion limits even on adversarial sorted-`low` inserts. This is *different* from the platform's point-keyed ordered maps (Splay/P133, Treap/P113, Skip List/P78): it answers *range-intersection* queries via the subtree-`max` augmentation. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a brute-force scan matched `overlap`/`stab`/`overlap_any` over 300 queries**, the **subtree-`max` invariant held through 6 000 random insert/remove ops**, and **15 000 ascending inserts completed with no `RecursionError`** and a correct overlap query. Exposed at `/api/v1/intervaltree`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/interval_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- Ôťů 137A: `pradyos/core/interval_tree.py` ÔÇö `IntervalTreeError(detail)`; `IntervalTree()` with `insert(low, high)` (duplicates allowed), `remove(low, high)` Ôćĺ bool, `contains(low, high)`, `overlap_any(low, high)` Ôćĺ `(low,high)`|None, `overlap(low, high)` Ôćĺ sorted list, `stab(point)` Ôćĺ sorted list, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `max_endpoint` properties + `height()` + `stats()`. Endpoints must be numbers with `low ÔëĄ high` (bools and non-numerics raise `IntervalTreeError`). Insert/remove are iterative with bottom-up `max` fixup along the path; queries prune via subtree-`max`.
- Ôťů 137B: `pradyos/web/interval_tree_web.py` ÔÇö `register_intervaltree_routes(app, interval_tree=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/intervaltree/insert` (body `{low, high}`; 422 on missing / `low>high` / non-numeric), `DELETE /api/v1/intervaltree/remove` (body `{low, high}` Ôćĺ `{removed, size}`), `GET /api/v1/intervaltree/overlap` (query `?low=&high=`), `GET /api/v1/intervaltree/stab` (query `?point=`), `GET /api/v1/intervaltree/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/intervaltree/reset` (`overlap_any` / `contains` stay on the core class).
- Ôťů 137C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase137.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `interval_tree` param, and a single `register_intervaltree_routes(app, interval_tree)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- Ôťů 137D: `tests/test_interval_tree.py` (33) + `tests/test_intervaltree_web.py` (23) ÔÇö **a differential test against brute force** for `overlap`/`stab`/`overlap_any` + a 6 000-op random insert/remove sequence holding the **`max`-augmentation invariant**; **adversarial 15 000 sorted inserts** (no recursion error); inclusive-endpoint overlap, single-point & negative intervals, duplicates, `remove` (root / two-children / absent); validation (`low>high`, bool, non-numeric, non-numeric `stab`) + `IntervalTreeError.detail`; reset; `max_endpoint` / height / determinism; 10-thread concurrent inserts; all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `skewheap`).

**Phase 138 ÔÇö Complete.** All 293 test modules green. Sovereign Sparse Table (Bender & Farach-Colton) ÔÇö a **static range-minimum/maximum index answering queries in `O(1)`** after `O(n log n)` preprocessing, a new capability for the platform. It precomputes `table[k][i] = aggregate of the 2ßÁĆ elements starting at i`, so any half-open range `[lo, hi)` is covered by **two overlapping power-of-two blocks** ÔÇö `op(table[k][lo], table[k][hiÔłĺ2ßÁĆ])` with `k = ÔîŐlogÔéé(hiÔłĺlo)Ôîő` ÔÇö a constant-time query, exact because `min`/`max` are **idempotent** (`op(x,x)=x`) so the overlap is harmless. This is *different* from the platform's *dynamic* Segment Tree (P81), which supports updates with `O(log n)` queries: a sparse table is **static** (built once, no updates) but answers in `O(1)`, the right tradeoff for immutable data. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against brute-force `min`/`max` matched every one of the `O(n┬▓)` ranges for both ops across array sizes 1ÔÇŽ100**, plus 2 000 random queries on a 5 000-element array. Exposed at `/api/v1/sparsetable`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic (static ÔÇö built once from the array). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/sparse_table_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- Ôťů 138A: `pradyos/core/sparse_table.py` ÔÇö `SparseTableError(detail)`; `SparseTable(values=None, op="min")` with `build(values, op=None)` (static rebuild), `query(lo, hi)` (half-open `[lo, hi)`, `O(1)`), `get(i)`, `reset(op=None)`, `__len__`, and `size` / `op` / `levels` properties + `stats()`. `op Ôłł {min, max}`; values must be numbers (bools/non-numerics rejected); `query` needs `0 ÔëĄ lo < hi ÔëĄ n` and `get` needs `0 ÔëĄ i < n` ÔÇö all violations raise `SparseTableError` (non-int indices rejected). `k = (hiÔłĺlo).bit_length()Ôłĺ1` gives `ÔîŐlogÔééÔîő` in O(1).
- Ôťů 138B: `pradyos/web/sparse_table_web.py` ÔÇö `register_sparsetable_routes(app, sparse_table=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/sparsetable/build` (body `{values[], op?}`; 422 on missing / bad value / bad op), `GET /api/v1/sparsetable/query` (query `?lo=&hi=`, `Query(ge=0/1)`), `GET /api/v1/sparsetable/get` (query `?i=`), `GET /api/v1/sparsetable/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/sparsetable/reset`.
- Ôťů 138C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase138.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `sparse_table` param, and a single `register_sparsetable_routes(app, sparse_table)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- Ôťů 138D: `tests/test_sparse_table.py` (33) + `tests/test_sparsetable_web.py` (21) ÔÇö **a differential test against brute force** for every range (both `min` and `max`) across sizes 1ÔÇŽ100 + 2 000 queries on a 5 000-element array; edges (single element, full range, adjacent, idempotent overlap, negatives, duplicates, floats); query/get bound checks (raise + `Query(ge=ÔÇŽ)` 422s, non-int rejected); build validation (bad value, bad op, non-iterable) + `SparseTableError.detail`; build replaces & op change; reset; `op`/`levels` properties; determinism; 10-thread concurrent read queries; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `intervaltree`).
- Ôťů 138E: `scripts/prove.py` ÔÇö 293 test modules registered (Phase 138 appends `test_sparse_table.py` + `test_sparsetable_web.py`).

**Phase 139 ÔÇö Complete.** All 295 test modules green. Sovereign KD-Tree (Bentley, 1975) ÔÇö a **k-dimensional spatial index** for nearest-neighbour and orthogonal range search, the platform's first *spatial* structure. Points are stored in a binary tree that **cycles through the dimensions by depth** (axis = depth mod k) and is built by **median split** per axis (so it stays balanced, height `O(log n)`). `nearest(point)` descends toward the query, then **backtracks, pruning any subtree whose splitting plane is farther than the best squared distance found** (that branch cannot hold a closer point ÔÇö comparisons use squared distance, no `sqrt`); `range(lo, hi)` reports all points inside the inclusive axis-aligned box, pruning a child when the box does not cross its splitting plane. This is *different* from the platform's one-dimensional ordered maps and interval tree ÔÇö it answers *multidimensional proximity* queries. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test confirmed `nearest` matched the brute-force minimum distance over 1 600 queries (k = 2 and 3, across many random point sets, compared by distance to allow ties)** and `range` matched a brute-force box scan; `k = 1` and `k = 4`, duplicates, single/empty all check out. Exposed at `/api/v1/kdtree`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic (static ÔÇö built once, median-split per axis). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/kd_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- Ôťů 139A: `pradyos/core/kd_tree.py` ÔÇö `KDTreeError(detail)`; `KDTree(points=None, dim=2)` with `build(points)` (static rebuild), `nearest(point)` Ôćĺ point|None, `nearest_dist(point)` Ôćĺ float|None, `range(lo, hi)` Ôćĺ sorted points, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `dim` properties + `height()` + `stats()`. `dim` a positive int; every point/query must have `dim` numeric coordinates; `range` needs `lo[i] ÔëĄ hi[i]` ÔÇö violations raise `KDTreeError`. NN backtracking prunes by `diff┬▓ < best┬▓`; range prunes per axis.

**Phase 140 ÔÇö Complete.** All 297 test modules green. Sovereign Radix Tree / Patricia Trie (Morrison, 1968) ÔÇö a **path-compressed prefix tree** for string keys, a new capability for the platform and a distinct, more compact cousin of the plain Trie (P83). Where a trie stores one character per edge, a radix tree **labels each edge with a whole substring** and collapses any chain of single-child nodes, so the node count is bounded by the number of distinguishing prefixes, not total key length ÔÇö the structure behind IP routing tables and autocomplete. `insert` **splits** an edge when a key diverges partway along it; `delete` clears the key and **re-merges** a now-only-child node back into its parent; `prefix_search(prefix)` returns every key under a prefix; `longest_prefix(query)` returns the longest stored key that is a prefix of `query` (the routing-table lookup). This is *different* from P83's character-per-edge trie: edge compression makes it space-efficient and yields `longest_prefix` directly. The reported `compression_ratio` is the honest one ÔÇö **characters stored per node** (a plain trie stores ~1). **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against `dict` matched `search` across a 15 000-op random insert/delete/search mix**, and `prefix_search` / `longest_prefix` matched brute-force scans; the prefix-of-another and delete-then-re-merge edge cases hold, and a shared-prefix set reports `compression_ratio Ôëł 2.1`. Exposed at `/api/v1/radixtree`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/radix_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- Ôťů 140A: `pradyos/core/radix_tree.py` ÔÇö `RadixTreeError(detail)`; `RadixTree(seed=0)` with `insert(key, value=None)`, `search(key)`, `contains` / `__contains__`, `delete(key)` Ôćĺ bool (with re-merge), `prefix_search(prefix)` Ôćĺ sorted `(key, value)` list, `longest_prefix(query)` Ôćĺ key|None, `keys()`, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `seed` properties + `num_nodes()` + `stats()` (`num_keys` / `num_nodes` / `compression_ratio` = chars-per-node). Non-string keys/prefixes (and non-int `seed`) raise `RadixTreeError`.
- Ôťů 140B: `pradyos/web/radix_tree_web.py` ÔÇö `register_radixtree_routes(app, radix_tree=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/radixtree/insert` (body `{key, value?}`; 422 on missing / non-str), `POST /api/v1/radixtree/search` (body `{key}` Ôćĺ `{found, value}`), `POST /api/v1/radixtree/prefix_search` (body `{prefix}` Ôćĺ `{results, count}`), `DELETE /api/v1/radixtree/delete` (body `{key}` Ôćĺ `{deleted, size}`), `GET /api/v1/radixtree/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/radixtree/reset` (`longest_prefix` / `contains` stay on the core class).
- Ôťů 140C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase140.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `radix_tree` param, and a single `register_radixtree_routes(app, radix_tree)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- Ôťů 140D: `tests/test_radix_tree.py` (35) + `tests/test_radix_tree_web.py` (22) ÔÇö **a differential test against `dict`** for insert/search across 2 000 inserts and an 8 000-op insert/delete/search mix; `prefix_search` & `longest_prefix` vs brute force (incl. IP-routing-style); edge split, empty key, prefix-of-another, delete-with-re-merge / re-insert / delete-non-key-internal; `compression_ratio > 1`, `num_nodes`; validation (non-str key/prefix, bad seed) + `RadixTreeError.detail`; reset; determinism; 10-thread concurrent inserts; all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `kdtree`).
- Ôťů 140E: `scripts/prove.py` ÔÇö 297 test modules registered (Phase 140 appends `test_radix_tree.py` + `test_radix_tree_web.py`).

**Phase 141 ÔÇö Complete.** All 299 test modules green. Sovereign Suffix Array (Manber & Myers, 1990) ÔÇö a **sorted index of all suffixes of a string** that answers substring queries by binary search, a new text-indexing capability that pairs with the Wavelet Tree (P135) and Radix Tree (P140). The array holds the starting positions of every suffix in lexicographic order; because all occurrences of a pattern share a common prefix, they form a **contiguous block** in that order, found by two binary searches (lower/upper bound) ÔÇö so `contains`, `count`, and `positions` are `O(m log n)`. An accompanying **LCP** array records adjacencies, from which the number of **distinct substrings** falls out as `n(n+1)/2 Ôłĺ ╬ú LCP`. This is *different* from the platform's prefix trees ÔÇö a suffix array indexes *every substring* of one text. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against brute-force scans matched `count`, `positions`, `contains`, the LCP array, and `distinct_substrings` across 37 texts** (incl. `banana`, `mississippi`, repeated chars, random); overlapping matches (`"aa"` in `"aaaa"` Ôćĺ 3), full-text and absent patterns, single-char and empty-text edges all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/suffixarray`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic (static ÔÇö built once from the text). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/suffix_array_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- Ôťů 141A: `pradyos/core/suffix_array.py` ÔÇö `SuffixArrayError(detail)`; `SuffixArray(text="")` with `build(text)` (static rebuild), `contains(pattern)`, `count(pattern)`, `positions(pattern)` (sorted), `suffix_array()`, `lcp_array()`, `distinct_substrings()`, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `text` properties + `stats()`. Non-string text/pattern and empty patterns raise `SuffixArrayError`; queries are two binary searches over the suffix array.
- Ôťů 141B: `pradyos/web/suffix_array_web.py` ÔÇö `register_suffixarray_routes(app, suffix_array=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/suffixarray/build` (body `{text}`; 422 on missing / non-str), `POST /api/v1/suffixarray/search` (body `{pattern}` Ôćĺ `{contains, count, positions}`; 422 on empty/missing), `GET /api/v1/suffixarray/array` (`{suffix_array, lcp_array}`), `GET /api/v1/suffixarray/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/suffixarray/reset`.
- Ôťů 141C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase141.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `suffix_array` param, and a single `register_suffixarray_routes(app, suffix_array)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- Ôťů 141D: `tests/test_suffix_array.py` (33) + `tests/test_suffix_array_web.py` (19) ÔÇö **a differential test against brute force** for SA-is-sorted-permutation, `count`/`positions`/`contains`, LCP, and `distinct_substrings` across 37 texts; specific values (`banana` SA = `[5,3,1,0,4,2]`, distinct = 15), overlapping counts, single-char/repeated/unicode, pattern-longer-than-text, absent; validation (empty / non-str pattern, non-str text) + `SuffixArrayError.detail`; build replaces; reset; determinism; 10-thread concurrent queries; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `radixtree`).

**Phase 142 ÔÇö Complete.** All 301 test modules green. Sovereign Aho-Corasick (Aho & Corasick, 1975) ÔÇö a **multi-pattern string-matching automaton** that finds *all* occurrences of *all* patterns in a text in a single `O(text + matches)` pass, a new capability for the platform. A trie of the patterns is augmented (by a BFS sweep) with **failure links** ÔÇö on a mismatch the link jumps to the longest proper suffix that is still a trie node, so the text is never re-scanned (KMP generalised to a *set* of patterns) ÔÇö and **output sets** that chain every pattern ending at a state via the failure path, so overlapping and nested matches are all reported. `add(pattern)` / `add_many`, `build()` (finalise links; also done lazily on first search), `search(text)` Ôćĺ sorted `(pattern, end_index)` matches, plus `count` / `contains_any`. This is *different* from the platform's single-string indexes (Suffix Array/P141, Radix Tree/P140): it matches a *dictionary* against a stream at once. **Verified** (honest): the **failure-link construction was differential-tested against a brute-force multi-find over 300 random pattern-sets**, and the textbook `{he, she, his, hers}` over `"ushers"` yields exactly `[(he,3),(she,3),(hers,5)]`; overlapping (`"aa"`├Ś3 in `"aaaa"`), nested, suffix-via-failure-link, dedup, and auto-build-on-search all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/ahocorasick`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/aho_corasick_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- Ôťů 142A: `pradyos/core/aho_corasick.py` ÔÇö `AhoCorasickError(detail)`; `AhoCorasick()` with `add(pattern)` Ôćĺ bool (dedup), `add_many(patterns)` Ôćĺ count, `build()`, `search(text)` Ôćĺ sorted `(pattern, end_index)` list, `count(text)`, `contains_any(text)`, `patterns()`, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `num_patterns` / `built` properties + `stats()`. Non-string / empty patterns and non-string text raise `AhoCorasickError`; the automaton auto-builds on the first search after a pattern is added (re-adding marks it dirty again).
- Ôťů 142B: `pradyos/web/aho_corasick_web.py` ÔÇö `register_ahocorasick_routes(app, aho_corasick=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/ahocorasick/add` (body `{pattern}`; 422 on missing / empty / non-str), `POST /api/v1/ahocorasick/add_many` (body `{patterns[]}`), `POST /api/v1/ahocorasick/search` (body `{text}` Ôćĺ `{matches, count}`), `GET /api/v1/ahocorasick/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/ahocorasick/reset`.

Existing routes untouched.
- Ôťů 142D: `tests/test_aho_corasick.py` (33) + `tests/test_aho_corasick_web.py` (20) ÔÇö the classic `ushers` example, nested & substring-of-another patterns, unicode; **a differential test against brute force over 300 random pattern-sets**; overlapping count, `contains_any`, single-char patterns, suffix-match-via-failure-link; edges (no patterns, empty text, absent, pattern-longer); dedup + add/dup return values; auto-build / re-add-marks-dirty / explicit build; `add_many`; validation (non-str / empty pattern, non-str text, non-iterable) + `AhoCorasickError.detail`; reset; `patterns()` sorted; determinism; 10-thread concurrent search; all 5 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `suffixarray`).

**Phase 143 ÔÇö Complete.** All 303 test modules green. Sovereign Binary (XOR) Trie ÔÇö a **bitwise trie over fixed-width integers** that answers **maximum-XOR** queries greedily, a new capability for the platform. Each integer is stored as a root-to-leaf path of its bits from the most significant down (`width` levels, default 32); `max_xor(q)` walks the trie preferring, at every level, the child whose bit is *opposite* to `q`'s (maximising that XOR bit), so a single `O(width)` descent finds `max(q ^ x)` over all stored `x`. With per-node counts (a multiset) it also supports `min_xor`, `count_xor_less(q, k)` (stored values whose XOR with `q` is `< k` ÔÇö the building block of XOR range queries), `insert`, `remove` (pruning emptied subtrees), and `contains`. This is *different* in mechanism from the character trie (P83) and radix tree (P140): a fixed-depth *binary* trie keyed on bit position ÔÇö the structure behind max-XOR-pair and XOR-range problems. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test matched `max_xor` / `min_xor` / `count_xor_less` / `contains` against brute force over 1 800 queries (widths 4ÔÇô32)** and an 8 000-op insert/remove multiset against a `Counter`; the classic max-XOR-pair (`max over x of max_xor(x)`) equals the brute-force best pair. Exposed at `/api/v1/xortrie`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; every operation iterative. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/xor_trie_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- Ôťů 143A: `pradyos/core/xor_trie.py` ÔÇö `XorTrieError(detail)`; `XorTrie(width=32)` with `insert(value)`, `remove(value)` Ôćĺ bool, `contains` / `__contains__`, `max_xor(query)` / `min_xor(query)` (raise on empty), `count_xor_less(query, k)`, `reset(width=None)`, `__len__`, and `size` / `width` properties + `stats()`. `width Ôłł [1, 256]`; values/queries must be ints in `[0, 2^width)`; non-int `k` rejected ÔÇö all raise `XorTrieError` (bools rejected). Per-node counts make it a multiset.
- Ôťů 143B: `pradyos/web/xor_trie_web.py` ÔÇö `register_xortrie_routes(app, xor_trie=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/xortrie/insert` (body `{value}`; 422 on missing / out-of-range), `DELETE /api/v1/xortrie/remove` (body `{value}` Ôćĺ `{removed, size}`), `POST /api/v1/xortrie/query` (body `{query}` Ôćĺ `{max_xor, min_xor}`; 422 on empty trie), `POST /api/v1/xortrie/count_xor_less` (body `{query, k}`), `GET /api/v1/xortrie/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/xortrie/reset` (`contains` stays on the core class).
- Ôťů 143C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase143.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `xor_trie` param, and a single `register_xortrie_routes(app, xor_trie)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- Ôťů 143D: `tests/test_xor_trie.py` (33) + `tests/test_xor_trie_web.py` (22) ÔÇö **differential vs brute force** for `max_xor`/`min_xor`/`count_xor_less`/`contains` across widths 4ÔÇô32, an 8 000-op insert/remove multiset, and the **classic max-XOR-pair**; counted duplicates, `k` bounds, single value, empty raises; validation (`width`, out-of-range / negative / bool value, out-of-range query, non-int `k`) + `XorTrieError.detail`; reset / reconfigure width; `num_nodes`; determinism; 10-thread concurrent inserts; all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `ahocorasick`).

**Phase 144 ÔÇö Complete.** All 305 test modules green. Sovereign Min-Max Heap (Atkinson, Sack, Santoro & Strothotte, 1986) ÔÇö a **double-ended priority queue** giving `O(1)` access to *both* the minimum and the maximum and `O(log n)` `extract_min` / `extract_max`, a new capability for the platform (the Skew Heap of P136 is a min-only meldable queue). It is a single array-backed binary heap whose levels **alternate**: a node on an even (min) level is `ÔëĄ` all its descendants; on an odd (max) level it is `Ôëą` all theirs. Insertion bubbles up against *grandparents* on the matching level type; `extract_min` / `extract_max` sift down by repeatedly swapping with the smallest/largest among a node's children *and grandchildren* (with a parent fix-up when a grandchild is chosen) ÔÇö the level-parity logic that makes both ends cheap at once. Supports `push` / `push_many`, `peek_min` / `peek_max`, `extract_min` / `extract_max`, `keys_sorted`, `__len__`. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test confirmed `extract_min` yields ascending and `extract_max` descending order over 150 trials, an interleaved `extract_min`/`extract_max` mix matched a sorted deque over 100 trials, and the min-max invariant held through every push and extract**; level-boundary sizes 1ÔÇô5, a 2 000-element drain, duplicates and strings all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/minmaxheap`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; sift-down iterative. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/min_max_heap_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- Ôťů 144A: `pradyos/core/min_max_heap.py` ÔÇö `MinMaxHeapError(detail)`; `MinMaxHeap()` with `push(value)` / `push_many(values)` Ôćĺ count, `peek_min()` / `peek_max()` (raise on empty), `extract_min()` / `extract_max()` (raise on empty), `keys_sorted()`, `is_empty()`, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `kind` properties + `stats()`. Values must be one orderable kind (`int`/`float` or `str`); bools, non-orderable values and mixed kinds raise `MinMaxHeapError`. Level parity is `(i+1).bit_length()Ôłĺ1 mod 2`; bubble-up compares grandparents; sift-down scans children+grandchildren.
- Ôťů 144B: `pradyos/web/min_max_heap_web.py` ÔÇö `register_minmaxheap_routes(app, min_max_heap=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/minmaxheap/push` (body `{value}`; 422 on missing / bad / mixed-kind), `POST /api/v1/minmaxheap/extract_min` (422 on empty), `POST /api/v1/minmaxheap/extract_max` (422 on empty), `GET /api/v1/minmaxheap/peek` (`min`/`max` null when empty), `GET /api/v1/minmaxheap/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/minmaxheap/reset`.
- Ôťů 144C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase144.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `min_max_heap` param, and a single `register_minmaxheap_routes(app, min_max_heap)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- Ôťů 144D: `tests/test_min_max_heap.py` (32) + `tests/test_min_max_heap_web.py` (20) ÔÇö **differential vs sorted** for ascending/descending drains and **interleaved extract vs a sorted deque**, plus the **min-max invariant** through pushes and extracts; level-boundary sizes, 2 000-drain, duplicates, floats/negatives, strings; empty-op & validation raises (bool, non-orderable, mixed kind, non-iterable) + `MinMaxHeapError.detail`; `push_many`; `kind` resets when emptied; reset; determinism; 10-thread concurrent pushes; all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `xortrie`).

**Phase 145 ÔÇö Complete.** All 307 test modules green. Sovereign Cartesian Tree (Vuillemin, 1980) ÔÇö a **binary tree built from a sequence** that is simultaneously a **binary-search tree on position** and a **min-heap on value**, a new capability for the platform. It is constructed in `O(n)` by a single left-to-right scan with a stack (each new element pops larger-valued nodes off the right spine, adopts the last popped as its left child, becomes the right child of whatever remains), and its in-order traversal recovers the original index order. Its defining property is the **range-minimum Ôćö lowest-common-ancestor equivalence**: the minimum of any index range `[l, r]` is the value at the LCA of positions `l` and `r` (here via parent pointers + a depth array) ÔÇö so `range_min` is an LCA lookup, with leftmost-on-ties. Supports `build`, `range_min(l, r)` / `range_argmin`, `inorder`, `sequence`, and exposes the `structure` (parent/left/right arrays). This is *different* from the doubling-table Sparse Table (P138): the same range-min query, via an explicit tree that also underlies treap construction and suffix-tree links. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test confirmed `inorder == 0ÔÇŽn-1`, the BST+min-heap invariants, and `range_min` against a brute scan over *every* range across 120+ random sequences**; the root is the global argmin, ties take the leftmost, and a degenerate sorted 5 000-element input builds and queries with no recursion error. Exposed at `/api/v1/cartesiantree`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; every operation iterative. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/cartesian_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- Ôťů 145A: `pradyos/core/cartesian_tree.py` ÔÇö `CartesianTreeError(detail)`; `CartesianTree(values=None)` with `build(values)` (static rebuild), `range_min(lo, hi)` / `range_argmin(lo, hi)`, `inorder()`, `sequence()`, `structure()`, `reset()`, `__len__`, and `size` / `root_index` properties + `height()` + `stats()`. Values must be numbers (bools/non-numerics rejected); `range_min` needs `0 ÔëĄ lo ÔëĄ hi < n` (non-int rejected) ÔÇö all raise `CartesianTreeError`. Build is a stack; LCA is a parent-walk over a precomputed depth array.
- Ôťů 145B: `pradyos/web/cartesian_tree_web.py` ÔÇö `register_cartesiantree_routes(app, cartesian_tree=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/cartesiantree/build` (body `{values[]}`; 422 on missing / non-numeric), `GET /api/v1/cartesiantree/range_min` (query `?lo=&hi=`, `Query(ge=0)` Ôćĺ `{min, argmin}`), `GET /api/v1/cartesiantree/structure`, `GET /api/v1/cartesiantree/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/cartesiantree/reset`.

**Phase 146 ÔÇö Complete.** All 309 test modules green. Sovereign 2D Fenwick Tree (2D Binary Indexed Tree; Fenwick, 1994) ÔÇö a **2-D point-update / rectangle-sum index** in `O(log┬▓n)` per operation, a new capability for the platform (the Fenwick Tree of P80 is one-dimensional). Over an `R ├Ś C` grid each internal `(i, j)` holds the sum of a rectangle of cells fixed by the low-bits of `i` and `j`; `update(i, j, delta)` walks `i += i&-i`, `j += j&-j` and a prefix sum walks them down ÔÇö so the sum of any sub-rectangle is **four prefix sums** by inclusion-exclusion. Supports `update`, `point_value`, `prefix_sum(i, j)` (sum of `[0..i] ├Ś [0..j]`), `range_sum(r1, c1, r2, c2)`, and `total`. This is *different* from the 1-D Fenwick (P80) and the range-*min* structures (Sparse Table/P138, Cartesian Tree/P145): it answers 2-D rectangle *sum* queries under point updates. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a brute reference grid matched `prefix_sum`, `range_sum`, and `point_value` over 480 queries across six grid shapes** plus a 50├Ś50 grid with 3 000 updates; negatives/accumulation, full-grid, single row/column and 1├Ś1 edges all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/fenwick2d`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; every operation iterative. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/fenwick2d_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- Ôťů 146A: `pradyos/core/fenwick_2d.py` ÔÇö `Fenwick2DError(detail)`; `Fenwick2D(rows=16, cols=16)` with `update(i, j, delta)`, `prefix_sum(i, j)`, `range_sum(r1, c1, r2, c2)`, `point_value(i, j)`, `total()`, `reset(rows=None, cols=None)`, and `rows` / `cols` properties + `stats()`. `rows`/`cols` positive ints; coordinates ints in range; `delta` a number; `range_sum` needs `r1 ÔëĄ r2`, `c1 ÔëĄ c2` ÔÇö all violations raise `Fenwick2DError` (bools rejected). Updates and prefix sums are nested low-bit walks; `range_sum` is inclusion-exclusion of four prefix sums.
- Ôťů 146B: `pradyos/web/fenwick2d_web.py` ÔÇö `register_fenwick2d_routes(app, fenwick2d=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/fenwick2d/update` (body `{i, j, delta}`; 422 on missing / out-of-range / bad delta), `GET /api/v1/fenwick2d/prefix_sum` (query `?i=&j=`, `Query(ge=0)`), `GET /api/v1/fenwick2d/range_sum` (query `?r1=&c1=&r2=&c2=`), `GET /api/v1/fenwick2d/point_value` (query `?i=&j=`), `GET /api/v1/fenwick2d/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/fenwick2d/reset` (body `{rows?, cols?}`).

**Phase 147 ÔÇö Complete.** All 311 test modules green. Sovereign Sqrt Decomposition ÔÇö a **block-decomposition range structure** supporting `O(ÔłÜn)` **range-add** and **range-sum** over an array, a new *technique* for the platform (distinct from Segment Tree/P81's `O(log n)` and the point-update Fenwick/P80). The array is split into `ÔëłÔłÜn` contiguous blocks, each carrying a block sum and a **lazy "add" tag** applied conceptually to every element of the block but not yet pushed down; the true value of element `i` is `a[i] + tag[block(i)]`. A range update touches the `O(ÔłÜn)` fully-covered blocks via their tags (`tag[b] += delta`) and the two partial boundary blocks element-wise (updating both the element and its block sum); a range query sums each covered block's `block_sum + tag┬Ěblock_len` plus the partial ends ÔÇö both `O(ÔłÜn)`. Supports `range_add(lo, hi, delta)`, `range_sum(lo, hi)`, `point_query(i)`, absolute point `update(i, value)`, `build`, `total`, and `reset`. This is *different* from the platform's other range structures: a deliberately simple `O(ÔłÜn)` block method with lazy tags ÔÇö the classic stepping-stone to segment-tree lazy propagation. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a brute reference array matched `range_sum` and `point_query` over 349 random queries across nine array sizes** plus a 1 000-element / 500-update differential; exact-block / spanning / within-one-block / whole-array ranges, update interacting with an active tag, negative deltas, 1-element and float arrays all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/sqrtdecomp`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; every operation iterative. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/sqrt_decomposition_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- Ôťů 147A: `pradyos/core/sqrt_decomposition.py` ÔÇö `SqrtDecompositionError(detail)`; `SqrtDecomposition(values=None)` with `range_add(lo, hi, delta)`, `range_sum(lo, hi)`, `point_query(i)`, `update(i, value)`, `total()`, `build(values)`, `reset()`, `len()` / `size` / `block_size` / `num_blocks` + `stats()`. `values` numbers; indices ints in range; `lo ÔëĄ hi`; `delta` / `value` numbers ÔÇö all violations raise `SqrtDecompositionError` (bools rejected). `block_size = ÔîŐÔłÜnÔîő`; covered blocks updated via a lazy tag, partial boundary blocks element-wise; every operation iterative.

**Phase 148 ÔÇö Complete.** All 313 test modules green. Sovereign Li Chao Tree ÔÇö a **line container** over a fixed integer x-domain `[x_min, x_max]` that maintains a set of lines `y = m┬Ěx + b` and answers the **minimum (or maximum) `y` at any query `x`** in `O(log C)` (`C = x_max Ôłĺ x_min + 1`), the segment-tree "Li Chao" form of the convex-hull-trick / kinetic line container ÔÇö the platform's *first* line-container structure. It is an implicit segment tree over the x-range; each node owns the line dominant at its segment midpoint, and `add_line` keeps the midpoint-winner at the node while pushing the loser into the *one* half-segment where it can still become dominant, and `query(x)` takes the best value among the lines on the rootÔćĺleaf path for `x`. Max-mode is served by the same min machinery via sign-flipped lines. This is *different* from every range-sum/range-min index (Fenwick/P80, Segment Tree/P81, Sparse Table/P138, Cartesian Tree/P145, 2D Fenwick/P146, Sqrt Decomposition/P147) and the spatial KD-Tree/P139: it answers linear-function extrema, not array aggregates. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a brute list of lines matched min-mode over 2 910 queries and max-mode over 2 400 queries** across 80 random line sets, and **every one of the 120 insertion-order permutations of a 5-line set produced identical query results** (the "push loser to the winnable half" logic is order-invariant); float lines, parallel/crossing lines, domain edges, single-point domain and the emptyÔćĺ`None` case all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/lichao`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; add/query descents iterative. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/li_chao_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- Ôťů 148A: `pradyos/core/li_chao_tree.py` ÔÇö `LiChaoTreeError(detail)`; `LiChaoTree(x_min=0, x_max=1_000_000, mode='min')` with `add_line(m, b)`, `query(x)`, `reset(x_min=None, x_max=None, mode=None)`, `len()` / `num_lines` / `x_min` / `x_max` / `mode` + `stats()`. `x_min ÔëĄ x_max` ints; `mode Ôłł {min, max}`; `m`/`b` numbers; `x` an int in domain ÔÇö all violations raise `LiChaoTreeError` (bools rejected). `query` returns `None` when no lines added. Implicit segment tree keyed by `(l, r)` in a dict; add/query iterative; max-mode via sign-flipped lines.
- Ôťů 148B: `pradyos/web/li_chao_tree_web.py` ÔÇö `register_lichao_routes(app, li_chao_tree=None)` mounts 5 routes: `POST /api/v1/lichao/add_line` (body `{m, b}`; 422 missing / non-num), `POST /api/v1/lichao/add_lines` (body `{lines: [[m, b], ÔÇŽ]}`; 422 bad shape / non-num), `GET /api/v1/lichao/query` (query `?x=`, negatives allowed; `value` may be null), `GET /api/v1/lichao/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/lichao/reset` (body `{x_min?, x_max?, mode?}`).

**Phase 149 ÔÇö Complete.** All 315 test modules green. Sovereign Persistent Segment Tree ÔÇö a **fully-persistent (versioned) range-sum index**: the array starts as *version 0*, and every point `update` returns a *new version* in `O(log n)` via **path-copying** (the `O(log n)` nodes on the rootÔćĺleaf path are copied while every untouched subtree is *shared* with the previous version), so any past version stays queryable forever in `O(log n)` and `k` updates cost only `O(k log n)` extra nodes. This is the platform's **first persistent / immutable data structure** ÔÇö distinct from every *ephemeral* range index (Fenwick/P80, Segment Tree/P81, Sparse Table/P138, 2D Fenwick/P146, Sqrt Decomposition/P147) and from the Li Chao line-container/P148: those keep one mutable state, this keeps the entire history. Nodes live in append-only parallel arrays (`_sum`/`_left`/`_right`) indexed by node-id and are never mutated after creation ÔÇö which is exactly what makes old versions safe. Supports `build(values)` Ôćĺ version 0, `update(version, i, value)` Ôćĺ a new version index, `range_sum(version, lo, hi)`, `point_query(version, i)`, and `num_versions`. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a list of per-version reference arrays matched `range_sum` and `point_query` over 1 275 queries on *every* version (including the oldest) after many updates** across nine sizes ÔÇö proving immutability / no aliasing ÔÇö plus a 200-element / 300-update differential, branching history (updating an old version twice), a 20-deep update chain, single-element / power-of-two / non-power-of-two shapes, floats and negatives. Exposed at `/api/v1/perseg`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; build / update / query all iterative. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/persistent_segment_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- Ôťů 149A: `pradyos/core/persistent_segment_tree.py` ÔÇö `PersistentSegmentTreeError(detail)`; `PersistentSegmentTree(values=None)` with `build(values)`, `update(version, i, value)` Ôćĺ new version index, `range_sum(version, lo, hi)`, `point_query(version, i)`, `reset()`, `size` / `num_versions` / `len()` + `stats()`. `values` non-empty numbers; `version` in range; indices ints in `[0, n)`; `lo ÔëĄ hi`; `value` a number ÔÇö all violations raise `PersistentSegmentTreeError` (bools rejected). Append-only node arrays; iterative post-order build, iterative path-copy update, iterative query.
- Ôťů 149B: `pradyos/web/persistent_segment_tree_web.py` ÔÇö `register_perseg_routes(app, persistent_segment_tree=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/perseg/build` (body `{values}`; 422 missing / empty / non-num), `POST /api/v1/perseg/update` (body `{version, i, value}`), `GET /api/v1/perseg/range_sum` (query `?version=&lo=&hi=`, `Query(ge=0)`), `GET /api/v1/perseg/point_query` (query `?version=&i=`), `GET /api/v1/perseg/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/perseg/reset`.

**Phase 150 ÔÇö Complete.** All 317 test modules green. Sovereign Pairing Heap (FredmanÔÇôSedgewickÔÇôSleatorÔÇôTarjan, 1986) ÔÇö a self-adjusting **mergeable min-priority-queue** whose distinguishing feature is **`decrease_key` in `O(log n)` amortized** (with `O(1)` `insert` / `find_min` / internal `meld`), a capability the platform's other heaps lack (the Skew Heap/P136 melds but exposes no key-decrease; the Min-Max Heap/P144 is double-ended but neither melds nor decreases keys). It is a single multiway tree kept min-at-root: `insert` melds in a one-node tree, `delete_min` removes the root and re-pairs its children with the classic **two-pass** merge (leftÔćĺright meld consecutive pairs, then rightÔćĺleft accumulate), and `decrease_key` lowers a node's value, detaches its subtree, and melds it back at the root. Nodes live in append-only parallel arrays (`_val`/`_child`/`_sibling`/`_parent`) indexed by a **stable integer handle** returned from `insert`, which is what makes `decrease_key` addressable. Supports `insert(value)` Ôćĺ handle, `find_min`, `find_min_handle`, `delete_min`, `decrease_key(handle, value)`, `size`, `is_empty`, and `reset`. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a brute `{handle Ôćĺ value}` dict matched `find_min` after every op over 4 800 random insert/delete_min/decrease_key operations**, and a **full-drain == `sorted` check across 60 random trials** plus a 3 000-element drain; decrease-to-new-min, decrease-the-root, decrease-to-same-value, duplicates, insertion-order independence, and dead/bad-handle rejection all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/pairingheap`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; iterative (two-pass delete-min, `O(1)` meld/detach). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/pairing_heap_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- Ôťů 150A: `pradyos/core/pairing_heap.py` ÔÇö `PairingHeapError(detail)`; `PairingHeap()` with `insert(value)` Ôćĺ handle, `find_min`, `find_min_handle`, `delete_min`, `decrease_key(handle, value)`, `is_empty`, `reset`, `size` / `len()` + `stats()`. `value` a number; `handle` a live int handle; `decrease_key` must not increase the value ÔÇö all violations raise `PairingHeapError` (bools rejected; empty `find_min`/`delete_min` raise). Append-only `_val`/`_child`/`_sibling`/`_parent` arrays; `O(1)` meld, iterative two-pass `delete_min`, sibling-walk `decrease_key` detach.
- Ôťů 150B: `pradyos/web/pairing_heap_web.py` ÔÇö `register_pairingheap_routes(app, pairing_heap=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/pairingheap/insert` (body `{value}`; 422 missing / non-num), `GET /api/v1/pairingheap/find_min` (`min` null when empty), `POST /api/v1/pairingheap/delete_min` (422 if empty), `POST /api/v1/pairingheap/decrease_key` (body `{handle, value}`; 422 bad/dead handle / key-increase), `GET /api/v1/pairingheap/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/pairingheap/reset`.

Existing routes untouched.

**Phase 151 ÔÇö Complete.** All 319 test modules green. Sovereign Suffix Automaton (Blumer et al. 1985 / Crochemore) ÔÇö the **minimal deterministic automaton recognizing every substring** of a string, built **online** in `O(n)` amortized by appending characters and splitting/cloning states along suffix links. Paths from the initial state spell exactly the substrings, so `contains` is an `O(|p|)` walk, and the **number of distinct substrings** is `╬ú (len[v] Ôłĺ len[link[v]])` over every non-initial state. This is the platform's first automaton-of-all-substrings ÔÇö distinct from the sorted-suffix index (Suffix Array/P141, which binary-searches sorted suffixes) and the multi-pattern failure-link trie (AhoÔÇôCorasick/P142, which scans for a fixed dictionary). States live in parallel `len`/`link`/`trans` lists (transitions are per-state dicts, so the alphabet may be ASCII or Unicode). Supports `extend(ch)` / `build(text)`, `contains(pattern)`, `distinct_substrings()`, `num_states`, `length`, and `reset`. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against the brute set of all substrings matched `distinct_substrings()` exactly across 300 random strings** (alphabets of 3 and 8, up to 60 chars) plus a 2 000-character string, and **`contains` matched brute membership over 1 500 queries** (substrings and non-substrings); `aaaa`Ôćĺ4, `abab`/`abcabc`/`banana`, single-char, empty, Unicode (`h├ęlloÔśâh├ęllo`), `num_states ÔëĄ 2n`, and `extend`-incremental == `build` all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/suffixautomaton`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; iterative online construction (no recursion). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/suffix_automaton_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

Parallel `_len`/`_link`/`_trans` lists; online suffix-link walk with state cloning, all `while`-loop iterative.

**Phase 152 ÔÇö Complete.** All 321 test modules green. Sovereign van Emde Boas Tree (van Emde Boas, 1975) ÔÇö a **bounded-integer ordered set over a universe `[0, U)`** (`U` rounded up to a power of two) supporting `insert` / `delete` / `member` / `minimum` / `maximum` and, most distinctively, **`successor` / `predecessor` in `O(log log U)`** ÔÇö a complexity class no existing platform structure offers, and the platform's first integer-universe (van-Emde-Boas-recursion) structure, distinct from comparison-ordered sets and from every hash/sketch. Each node recurses into a `ÔłÜU` *summary* plus up to `ÔłÜU` *clusters*, storing the running `min` **lazily** (the minimum is held outside its cluster) so every operation makes only one deep recursive call ÔÇö the `T(u) = T(ÔłÜu) + O(1)` recurrence. The recursion is carried by an internal lock-free node; the public class holds a single lock at the top so descent never re-enters it, and clusters/summaries are created lazily for `O(n)` memory. Supports `insert(x)` Ôćĺ added?, `delete(x)` Ôćĺ present?, `member(x)`, `minimum()`, `maximum()`, `successor(x)`, `predecessor(x)`, `size`, and `reset`. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a sorted-set ground truth matched `member` / `minimum` / `maximum` / `successor` / `predecessor` after every op over 20 960 query points across six universes**, an **exhaustive successor/predecessor sweep over all of `[0, 256)`**, and an **8 000-operation differential on `U = 65 536`**; duplicate-insert / delete-absent no-ops, single-element and boundary (`0`, `UÔłĺ1`) behaviour, universe rounding (`1000 Ôćĺ 1024`), full-universe successor walk and delete-min drain all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/veb`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; recursion depth is structurally bounded at `O(log log U) ÔëĄ ~5` (never input-dependent). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/van_emde_boas_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- Ôťů 152A: `pradyos/core/van_emde_boas.py` ÔÇö `VanEmdeBoasError(detail)`; `VanEmdeBoas(universe=65536)` with `insert(x)` Ôćĺ bool, `delete(x)` Ôćĺ bool, `member(x)`, `minimum()`, `maximum()`, `successor(x)`, `predecessor(x)`, `reset()`, `is_empty()`, `size` / `len()` / `universe` + `stats()`. `universe` a positive int (rounded up to a power of two); `x` an int in `[0, universe)` ÔÇö all violations raise `VanEmdeBoasError` (bools rejected). Internal lock-free `_VEBNode` recursion with lazy min and lazily-created summary/clusters; public methods take the lock once.
- Ôťů 152B: `pradyos/web/van_emde_boas_web.py` ÔÇö `register_veb_routes(app, van_emde_boas=None)` mounts 7 routes: `POST /api/v1/veb/insert` (body `{value}`), `POST /api/v1/veb/delete` (body `{value}`), `GET /api/v1/veb/member` (query `?value=`, `Query(ge=0)`), `GET /api/v1/veb/successor` (may be null), `GET /api/v1/veb/predecessor` (may be null), `GET /api/v1/veb/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/veb/reset`. Out-of-range / non-int Ôćĺ 422.

Existing routes untouched.

**Phase 153 ÔÇö Complete.** All 323 test modules green. Sovereign PR Quadtree (point-region quadtree; Finkel & Bentley, 1974) ÔÇö a **2-D spatial index over a fixed rectangle** storing *named* points, recursively subdividing a cell into four equal quadrants whenever a leaf would exceed one point (down to `max_depth`). It answers exact lookup, **axis-aligned rectangle range queries**, and **nearest-neighbour** (Euclidean, branch-and-bound over a min-heap of node lower-bounds), with dynamic insert/delete and cell collapse on delete ÔÇö the platform's first space-subdivision-by-quadrant structure, distinct from the median-split KD-Tree/P139 (a static nearest-neighbour index over the points): the quadtree subdivides *space*. A side `id Ôćĺ (x, y)` index gives O(1) delete/move. Subdivision depth is bounded by `max_depth` (never input-dependent), so descent is a bounded loop and range/nearest queries use an explicit stack / min-heap (no recursion). Supports `insert(point_id, x, y)` (move on duplicate id), `delete(point_id)`, `search(x, y)`, `range_query(x_min, y_min, x_max, y_max)`, `nearest(x, y)`, `num_points`, and `reset`. **Verified** (honest): **`range_query` matched a brute point set across 30+ random sub-rectangles of a 100├Ś100 grid**, **`nearest` matched brute min-Euclidean over 150 queries** (1 000- and 500-point clouds, incl. after deletes), full-bounds returns all 1 000 inserted, delete-all collapses the tree to a single root node, move-on-duplicate-id, coincident-point buckets at `max_depth`, and determinism (same seed Ôćĺ identical tree) all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/prquadtree`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic. Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/pr_quadtree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- Ôťů 153A: `pradyos/core/pr_quadtree.py` ÔÇö `PRQuadtreeError(detail)`; `PRQuadtree(x_min, y_min, x_max, y_max, max_depth=12)` with `insert(point_id, x, y)`, `delete(point_id)` Ôćĺ bool, `search(x, y)`, `range_query(...)` Ôćĺ sorted ids, `nearest(x, y)`, `reset()`, `num_points` / `len()` + `stats()`. Bounds must satisfy `x_min<x_max`, `y_min<y_max`; `max_depth Ôëą 1`; points must be numeric and in-bounds; `point_id` hashable / non-None ÔÇö violations raise `PRQuadtreeError`. Bounded-depth descent; explicit-stack range query; min-heap branch-and-bound nearest; collapse-on-delete.
- Ôťů 153B: `pradyos/web/pr_quadtree_web.py` ÔÇö `register_pr_quadtree_routes(app, pr_quadtree=None)` mounts 7 routes: `POST /api/v1/prquadtree/insert` (body `{point_id, x, y}`), `POST /api/v1/prquadtree/delete` (body `{point_id}`), `GET /api/v1/prquadtree/search` (`?x=&y=`), `GET /api/v1/prquadtree/range_query` (`?x_min=&y_min=&x_max=&y_max=`), `GET /api/v1/prquadtree/nearest` (`?x=&y=`, may be null), `GET /api/v1/prquadtree/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/prquadtree/reset`. Out-of-bounds / non-num / inverted-rect Ôćĺ 422.

**Phase 154 ÔÇö Complete.** All 325 test modules green. Sovereign Fibonacci Heap (Fredman & Tarjan, 1984) ÔÇö a **mergeable min-priority-queue with `O(1)` amortized `insert` / `find_min` / `decrease_key` and `O(log n)` amortized `extract_min`**, the asymptotically optimal heap behind Dijkstra/Prim. It is a forest of heap-ordered trees with a min-pointer; `extract_min` **consolidates** roots of equal degree (linking the larger-key root under the smaller via a degree array until all root degrees are distinct), and `decrease_key` **cuts** a node to the root list with **cascading cuts** up through already-marked ancestors ÔÇö a different mechanism from the two-pass Pairing Heap/P150 (and unlike the meld-only Skew Heap/P136 or the double-ended Min-Max Heap/P144). Nodes are objects in circular doubly-linked sibling lists; a stable integer handle from `insert` (mapped to its node) makes `decrease_key` addressable. Supports `insert(value)` Ôćĺ handle, `find_min`, `find_min_handle`, `extract_min`, `decrease_key(handle, value)`, `size`, `is_empty`, and `reset`. **Verified** (honest): a **full-drain == `sorted` check across 60 random trials** plus a 5 000-element drain, a **differential test against a brute `{handle Ôćĺ value}` dict matched `find_min` after every op over 10 000 random insert/extract_min/decrease_key operations**, and a **dedicated cascading-cut stress** (extract to force consolidation into deep trees, then 80 `decrease_key`s) ÔÇö find_min and the final drain both correct; decrease-to-new-min, duplicates, floats/negatives, insertion-order independence, and dead/bad-handle rejection all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/fibonacci`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; iterative consolidate + cascading cut (no recursion). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/fibonacci_heap_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- Ôťů 154A: `pradyos/core/fibonacci_heap.py` ÔÇö `FibonacciHeapError(detail)`; `FibonacciHeap()` with `insert(value)` Ôćĺ handle, `find_min`, `find_min_handle`, `extract_min`, `decrease_key(handle, value)`, `is_empty`, `reset`, `size` / `len()` + `stats()`. `value` a number; `handle` a live int handle; `decrease_key` must not increase the value ÔÇö all violations raise `FibonacciHeapError` (bools rejected; empty `find_min`/`extract_min` raise). Circular doubly-linked root/child lists; iterative degree-array consolidate and iterative cascading cut.
- Ôťů 154B: `pradyos/web/fibonacci_heap_web.py` ÔÇö `register_fibonacci_routes(app, fibonacci_heap=None)` mounts 6 routes: `POST /api/v1/fibonacci/insert` (body `{value}`), `GET /api/v1/fibonacci/find_min` (`min` null when empty), `POST /api/v1/fibonacci/extract_min` (422 if empty), `POST /api/v1/fibonacci/decrease_key` (body `{handle, value}`; 422 bad/dead handle / key-increase), `GET /api/v1/fibonacci/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/fibonacci/reset`.

Existing routes untouched.
- Ôťů 154D: `tests/test_fibonacci_heap.py` (35) + `tests/test_fibonacci_heap_web.py` (17) ÔÇö **a differential test against a brute `{handleÔćĺvalue}` dict** (10 000 mixed ops, using `find_min_handle` to stay exactly in sync) + full-drain == `sorted` (60 trials) + 5 000-element drain + a cascading-cut stress; decrease-to-new-min / decrease-root, duplicates, floats/negatives, insertion-order independence; validation (empty pop, non-num, bad/dead/non-int handle, key-increase, bool) + `FibonacciHeapError.detail`; reset; determinism; 4-thread concurrent inserts; all 6 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `prquadtree`).
- Ôťů 154E: `scripts/prove.py` ÔÇö 325 test modules registered (Phase 154 appends `test_fibonacci_heap.py` + `test_fibonacci_heap_web.py`).

**Phase 155 ÔÇö Complete.** All 327 test modules green. Sovereign AVL Tree (Adelson-Velsky & Landis, 1962) ÔÇö a **height-balanced comparison-ordered set** with *guaranteed* `O(log n)` `insert` / `delete` / `contains` / `successor` / `predecessor` / `min` / `max`, kept balanced by tracking each node's subtree height and applying single/double rotations whenever a node's balance factor leaves `{Ôłĺ1, 0, +1}`. Unlike the platform's other search trees it is *strictly* balanced on every update ÔÇö distinct from the amortized Splay Tree/P133, the randomized Treap, the RMQ Cartesian Tree/P145, and the integer-universe vEB/P152 (AVL orders *any* mutually-comparable keys: ints, floats, strings; duplicates ignored; `successor`/`predecessor` work for keys not present). Supports `insert(key)`, `delete(key)`, `contains(key)`, `successor(key)`, `predecessor(key)`, `minimum()`, `maximum()`, `in_order()`, `height()`, `size`, and `reset`. **Verified** (honest): a **differential test against a sorted reference set matched `in_order == sorted`, `contains`, `successor`/`predecessor` (1 840 point checks) and min/max across 40 random insert/delete trials, with the AVL balance invariant (`|bf| ÔëĄ 1` and stored heights correct at every node) re-checked after each trial**; the height stayed `ÔëĄ 1.44 logÔéé(n+2)` even under 5 000 *sorted* and *reverse-sorted* insertions (the naive-BST worst case), and sorted-delete-half, string/float keys, and duplicate-ignoring all hold. Exposed at `/api/v1/avl`. Pure stdlib; thread-safe via a single `threading.Lock`; deterministic; recursion depth structurally bounded at `ÔëĄ 1.44 logÔéé n` (the AVL height bound ÔÇö never degenerate). Routes live in their own `pradyos/web/avl_tree_web.py` module, wired into `create_app()` factory scope:

- Ôťů 155A: `pradyos/core/avl_tree.py` ÔÇö `AVLTreeError(detail)`; `AVLTree()` with `insert(key)` Ôćĺ bool, `delete(key)` Ôćĺ bool, `contains(key)`, `successor(key)`, `predecessor(key)`, `minimum()`, `maximum()`, `in_order()`, `height()`, `reset()`, `is_empty()`, `size` / `len()` + `stats()`. Keys must be `int`/`float`/`str` (no bool/None); mixed-type comparisons raise `AVLTreeError`. Generic balance-factor `_rebalance` (single/double rotations) shared by insert and delete; iterative `in_order`.
- Ôťů 155B: `pradyos/web/avl_tree_web.py` ÔÇö `register_avl_routes(app, avl_tree=None)` mounts 7 routes: `POST /api/v1/avl/insert` (body `{key}`, type-preserving), `POST /api/v1/avl/delete` (body `{key}`), `GET /api/v1/avl/contains` (`?key=`), `GET /api/v1/avl/successor` (may be null), `GET /api/v1/avl/predecessor` (may be null), `GET /api/v1/avl/stats`, `DELETE /api/v1/avl/reset`. Non-orderable / mixed-type Ôćĺ 422.
- Ôťů 155C: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` patched additively via `scripts/patch_web_phase155.py` (+4 lines: the import, the `avl_tree` param, and a single `register_avl_routes(app, avl_tree)` call before `return app`; the DASHBOARD_HTML line is asserted byte-length-unchanged; an `ast.parse` gate refuses to write broken code). Existing routes untouched.
- Ôťů 155D: `tests/test_avl_tree.py` (32) + `tests/test_avl_tree_web.py` (19) ÔÇö **a differential test against a sorted reference set** (40 trials) with the balance invariant re-checked each time; sorted/reverse 5 000-insert balance, sorted-delete-half, leaf/one-child/two-children delete, string & float keys, successor/predecessor boundaries + absent keys; validation (None, bool, unorderable, mixed-type) + `AVLTreeError.detail`; reset; determinism; 4-thread concurrent inserts; all 7 endpoints over HTTP incl. 422s + a prior-phase regression check (now incl. `fibonacci`).
- Ôťů 155E: `scripts/prove.py` ÔÇö 327 test modules registered (Phase 155 appends `test_avl_tree.py` + `test_avl_tree_web.py`).
- Ôťů 155F: README Phase Map updated; Phase 156 planned.

**Phase 156 ÔÇö Planned.** Sovereign B-Tree (Bayer & McCreight, 1972) ÔÇö a **multiway balanced search tree** of minimum degree `t` where every node holds between `tÔłĺ1` and `2tÔłĺ1` keys and all leaves sit at the same depth, the canonical database/filesystem index. It keeps perfect balance with `O(t logÔéť n)` `insert` / `delete` / `search`, splitting a full child *proactively* on the way down to insert and borrowing/merging to keep nodes at least half-full on delete ÔÇö a fundamentally different shape from every *binary* tree on the platform (AVL/P155, Splay/P133, Treap, Cartesian/P145). Supports `insert(key)`, `delete(key)`, `contains(key)`, `minimum()`, `maximum()`, `in_order()`, `height()`, `size`, and `reset`. To be exposed at `/api/v1/btree`; `b_tree` / `BTree` / `BTreeError` / `register_btree_routes` / `/api/v1/btree` verified free on `origin/main` (all `[0]`). Pure stdlib; thread-safe via `threading.Lock`; deterministic; recursion depth structurally bounded at `O(logÔéť n)`. Differential-tested against a sorted reference set; pivots to a Range Tree (also free) if B-tree delete cannot be reconstructed to the zero-flaw bar.

> *Phase-map note:* the Phase 132 slot was pre-verified for **AnchorHash**, but its `K`/`W`/`L`/`R` removal bookkeeping could not be reproduced to the platform's zero-flaw bar with confidence, so it was **pivoted** to the Cuckoo Hash Table (a fully-verifiable exact structure, differential-tested against `dict`). AnchorHash remains available for a future phase.

---

## PradyOS v0.41.0 ÔÇö Self-Driving

**99 test modules. 41 phases. Stdlib + asyncio only.**

A fully autonomous, self-driving OS kernel built in Python, with observe Ôćĺ alert Ôćĺ plan Ôćĺ react Ôćĺ heal Ôćĺ schedule Ôćĺ persist Ôćĺ remember Ôćĺ control-plane Ôćĺ heartbeat capabilities. The OS now drives itself ÔÇö `HeartbeatLoop` ticks `ControlPlane` on a fixed cadence, which in turn ticks the scheduler, healer, and reactor in sequence. No external orchestrator needed.

The OS observes its own metrics (`SignalAggregator`), detects thresholds (`WatchpointSystem`), correlates signals (`CorrelationEngine`), records every decision into a cryptographically chained ledger (`DecisionJournal`), reacts to alerts via rules (`ReactorEngine`), self-heals degraded components (`HealingMonitor`), schedules its own work (`TaskScheduler`), persists state across restarts (`SnapshotStore` + `StateManager`), remembers context with TTLs (`MemoryStore`), wires it all together (`SovereignBus`), exposes a unified introspection layer (`ControlPlane`), and drives itself forward through an async loop (`HeartbeatLoop`).

**Phase 15 ÔÇö Complete.** All 47 test modules green. Sovereign Scheduler ÔÇö cron-style recurring campaigns with priority queues and SLA-aware routing:
- Ôťů 15A: `pradyos/sovereign/scheduler.py` ÔÇö `SovereignScheduler` class with
  injectable `clock` for deterministic testing. Pure-stdlib 5-field cron parser
  supporting `*`, `*/N`, and single-integer fields for minute/hour/dom/month/dow.
  `next_run_after(cron_expr, after_ts)` scans minute-by-minute in UTC.
  `add_job()` stores job dicts with `job_id`, `cron_expr`, `campaign_spec`,
  `priority`, `sla_seconds`, `next_run`, `enabled`. `remove_job()` / `enable_job()`
  / `disable_job()` return bool. `tick()` fires all enabled jobs whose
  `next_run <= clock()`, publishes `"scheduler.job.fired"` bus events, advances
  `next_run`, and returns the list of fired job_ids. `start()` / `stop()` manage a
  daemon background thread; both are idempotent. Thread-safe via `threading.Lock`.
- Ôťů 15B: `pradyos/sovereign_web.py` ÔÇö five new endpoints wired via optional
  `scheduler` param in `create_app()`: `GET /api/v1/scheduler/jobs`,
  `POST /api/v1/scheduler/jobs`, `DELETE /api/v1/scheduler/jobs/{job_id}`,
  `POST /api/v1/scheduler/jobs/{job_id}/enable`,
  `POST /api/v1/scheduler/jobs/{job_id}/disable`. All return HTTP 200; safe
  empty responses when scheduler not injected.
- Ôťů 15C: `tests/test_sovereign_scheduler.py` ÔÇö 20 unit tests covering all
  scheduler methods, cron parsing, clock injection, bus event payload,
